# LogBrew SDK Readiness Memory

- 2026-06-29: Python SQLAlchemy automatic-engine span gap reduced after refreshed source reads from Sentry Python `getsentry/sentry-python@9c836062fc6f7244aae5046ce66814f0469c9891` (`sentry_sdk/integrations/sqlalchemy.py` `SqlalchemyIntegration.setup_once`, `_before_cursor_execute`, `_after_cursor_execute`, `_handle_error`), OpenTelemetry Python Contrib `open-telemetry/opentelemetry-python-contrib@ec27300a9433f5985cd7467ee840037e12602a70` (`instrumentation/opentelemetry-instrumentation-sqlalchemy/.../__init__.py`, `engine.py` `SQLAlchemyInstrumentor`, `EngineTracer`), and Datadog dd-trace-py `DataDog/dd-trace-py@8f36ac8332c5eb789f20241e547c486f51ade9be` (`ddtrace/contrib/internal/sqlalchemy/patch.py`, `engine.py` `trace_engine`, `EngineTracer._before_cur_exec`, `_after_cur_exec`, `_handle_db_error`). LogBrew now exports `instrument_sqlalchemy_engine_with_logbrew_spans(...)`: apps pass one owned SQLAlchemy engine, LogBrew imports SQLAlchemy only on opt-in, attaches only engine-local `before_cursor_execute`/`after_cursor_execute`/`handle_error` listeners, returns the existing instrumentation on duplicate calls, activates a child trace during cursor execution, emits sanitized DB spans, isolates capture failures, and removes listeners with `uninstall()`. Metadata is intentionally smaller than competitors: `framework=sqlalchemy`, DB system/operation, optional caller `dbName`, row count when non-negative, sampled state, primitive caller metadata after sensitive-key filtering, and type-only exceptions; it avoids global engine factory patching, sessions, raw SQL, SQL parameters, connection URLs, hosts/users, result rows, baggage, tracestate, exception messages, and stacks. Evidence: RED `PYTHONPATH=python/logbrew_py/src python3 -m unittest python/logbrew_py/tests/test_sqlalchemy_client.py` failed on missing export; GREEN focused 5 SQLAlchemy tests, full Python unit discovery ran 73 tests, `bash scripts/check_python_static.sh`, temp app with `SQLAlchemy>=2,<3`, full `bash scripts/real_user_python_smoke.sh` wheel/sdist install-remove-reinstall proof, ShellCheck 0.11.0, markdown links, backend contract reports, confidentiality scan, release metadata, generated-artifact hygiene, and Python syntax checks passed. No package release was made. Remaining Python gaps: DB-API auto coverage, global integration package options, Redis/Celery/RQ automatic hooks, DB metrics/pool/connect/fetch spans, SQL comments/obfuscation modes, richer semantic conventions, full OTel processor/exporter interop, baggage/tracestate, and broader framework-owned automatic instrumentation.
- 2026-06-29: Node MongoDB collection-span gap reduced after source reads from Sentry JS `getsentry/sentry-javascript@9730e1163e50e431f0d7db21ca3b8b0fb612fef8`, OpenTelemetry JS Contrib `open-telemetry/opentelemetry-js-contrib@eb98ccc85069304a1f0c2e6b33be1b2ca961b4be`, and Datadog dd-trace-js `DataDog/dd-trace-js@d1aa54a04b20570b1d8fb258e74266f97f652c11` MongoDB instrumentation paths. `@logbrew/node` now exports `instrumentLogBrewMongoCollection(...)` for app-owned MongoDB collection-like objects, wrapping supported collection operations plus cursor terminal methods such as `toArray()`/`next()` for `find()`/`aggregate()`, preserving Promise/sync results, rethrowing original errors, correlating with active request traces, rejecting duplicate installs, and uninstalling cleanly. Metadata includes `framework=node:mongodb`, `db.system.name=mongodb`, operation kind, optional database/collection names, sampled flag, W3C trace IDs, and bounded result counts; failures add type-only exception events. It avoids global MongoDB module or wire-protocol patching, connection-pool/session/connect hooks, filters, documents, raw command text, update specs, aggregation pipelines, comments, host/port/URL/connection strings, connection access values, baggage, tracestate, and raw propagation metadata. Evidence: RED installed smoke failed on missing MongoDB package/export surface; GREEN `bash scripts/real_user_node_smoke.sh` on Node `v22.18.0`, `npm test --prefix js/logbrew-node`, `python3 scripts/check_js_sources.py js/logbrew-node`, `bash scripts/check_js_lint.sh`, and `bash scripts/check_js_package.sh` passed; GitHub Actions CI run `28374578707` passed Contract, Swift, Kotlin, and Objective-C jobs for public SDK commit `9259f0ea`, including the Node.js real-user smoke and leak scan. Remaining MongoDB gaps: automatic driver instrumentation, wire-protocol spans, pool/connect/session metrics, Mongoose integration, DBM comments, query obfuscation modes, response hooks, heartbeat controls, callback-style legacy APIs, and broader semantic conventions.

Sentry/OTel inject W3C propagation through SNS/SQS message attributes; OTel exposes opt-in SQS payload extraction; Datadog additionally parses SNS and EventBridge envelopes and links batch receives while mutating producer payloads for richer automatic coverage. LogBrew now keeps the lighter explicit path: `extractLogBrewSqsTraceparent(...)`, `createLogBrewSqsTraceLinks(...)`, `sqsReceiveMessageWithLogBrewSpan(...)`, `withLogBrewSqsMessageProcessor(...)`, and `instrumentLogBrewSqsClient(...)` accept `extractSnsEnvelopeTraceparent`, `extractEventBridgeEnvelopeTraceparent`, and bounded `maxEnvelopeBytes`. - 2026-06-23: Apple platform grouping clarified from competitor source evidence. Sentry Cocoa `809ca17` `README.md`/`Package.swift` presents one Apple SDK with Swift and Objective-C setup under the same surface and same SwiftPM package family; Datadog iOS `9a17d2c` `README.md`/`Package.swift` presents one iOS/tvOS SDK with Swift and Objective-C libraries plus modular SwiftPM signal products; PostHog iOS `6e70aa2` `README.md`/`Package.swift` presents one iOS SDK with one `PostHog` SwiftPM product and an Objective-C example as a usage variant. LogBrew should therefore show one top-level Apple app setup path, preferably `iOS / Swift` for iOS-specific flows or `Apple / Swift` for broader Apple flows, and keep Objective-C as an advanced source/header variant. Public docs now reflect that SwiftPM `LogBrew` is the primary Apple path while `objc/logbrew-objc` remains separate source/header packaging; do not imply Objective-C installs through the Swift package until packaging changes.

- 2026-06-23: Browser auth-safe unload/offline delivery backend contract gap is now documented in `docs/backend-contracts/browser-delivery-2026-06-23.md` after source-backed comparison with Sentry JS `c5e245f`, Datadog Browser SDK `e387e04`, and PostHog JS `5486ab3`. - 2026-06-23: Browser lifecycle flush observability gap reduced after source re-checks of Sentry JS `c5e245f` browser `makeFetchTransport` pending keepalive limits, Datadog browser SDK `e387e04` exit-time send-beacon helper, and PostHog JS `5486ab3` `_sendBeacon`. `installLogBrewBrowser()` callbacks now receive `details.reason` as `capture`, `pagehide`, or `visibility_hidden`; installed browser fake-intake smoke proves fake `pagehide` dispatch flushes through packed packages, reports reason `pagehide`, clears the queue, uses the documented fetch header path for client-key delivery, and stops after `uninstall()`. LogBrew still intentionally avoids default `sendBeacon` because it cannot preserve the same header-based client-key delivery as `fetch`; unload/offline delivery remains weaker than Sentry/Datadog/PostHog.
- 2026-06-23: Public/non-public repository boundary tightened again. Keep public SDK behavior proof public when it is generic product evidence: SDK source, package metadata, README/API docs, examples, unit/contract tests, local fake-intake verifiers, installed-artifact smokes, release metadata checks, public backend contract reports, source-backed competitor research, and high-load local SDK tests. Do not move those into non-public suites merely to hide normal quality evidence. Keep live account/session/storage/dashboard/symbolication flows, real service endpoints, secret-backed E2E/load tests, live product telemetry, non-public logs/paths/plans, and customer-like data in non-public suites. Public SDK automation should stay aligned with non-public tests by consuming only redacted outcomes, backend contract drift, or generic verifier summaries; never copy non-public details into public files.
- 2026-06-23: JS/browser 429 rate-limit gap reduced after source re-checks of Sentry JS `c5e245f` `packages/core/src/utils/ratelimit.ts` (`parseRetryAfterHeader`, `updateRateLimits`) and `packages/core/src/transports/base.ts`, plus PostHog JS `5486ab3` request status callbacks. Core `flush()` now surfaces HTTP 429 as `SdkError` code `rate_limited`, preserves queued events, avoids immediate retry, and carries optional `retryAfterMs`; browser `createFetchTransport()` parses standard `Retry-After` seconds/date headers. - 2026-06-23: Browser keepalive delivery gap reduced after the existing Sentry/Datadog/PostHog browser transport source reads in `docs/competitor-research/browser-fake-intake-2026-06-22.md`. `@logbrew/browser` `createFetchTransport()` now defaults to a 64 KiB `maxKeepaliveBodyBytes` guard: oversized keepalive payloads fail before `fetch` with non-retryable `keepalive_body_too_large`, preserving queued events for a later explicit `keepalive: false` large-batch flush; fallback byte counting is UTF-8 accurate without `TextEncoder`. - 2026-06-11: Public severity docs now have a canonical `docs/severity-contract.md` source of truth. Keep LogBrew's product vocabulary at `info`, `warning`, `error`, and `critical`; treat `trace`, `debug`, `warn`, and `fatal` as SDK/runtime compatibility aliases only. Competitor comparison signal: Sentry exposes six levels including `debug` and `fatal`, while OpenTelemetry separates runtime severity text/number; LogBrew should stay simpler for user-facing product categories while preserving logger compatibility and canonical backend payloads. - 2026-06-11: Competitor install comparison documented at `docs/competitor-research/sentry-javascript-2026-06-11.md`. Fresh npm lockfile and registry checks showed `@logbrew/sdk@0.1.1` is dependency-free with 90,289 unpacked bytes/12 files, `@logbrew/browser@0.1.0` is dependency-free peer-only with 64,807 bytes/10 files, while `@sentry/browser@10.57.0` is 2,681,257 bytes/692 files with replay/feedback/core dependencies and `@sentry/node@10.57.0` is 3,889,201 bytes/1,071 files with OpenTelemetry/import-hook dependencies. Protect this lightweight install advantage; compete by making explicit W3C trace/action/network/session timelines easier and more agent-readable, not by copying heavyweight automatic instrumentation, global patching, visual replay, payload/header capture, or broad Sentry-style configuration.

They emit explicit `http.server.duration` histogram metrics with primitive low-cardinality metadata (`framework`, `method`, `routeTemplate`, `statusCode`, `statusCodeClass`), strip query/hash text, support metrics-only mode with successful request spans disabled, and preserve framework-owned responses plus existing trace/error behavior. - 2026-06-15: Rust HTTP server request telemetry gap reduced after reviewing Sentry Axum docs plus `getsentry/sentry-rust@e33b7ff`, OpenTelemetry Rust trace-context propagation source `8882149`, and Datadog Rust library docs. - 2026-06-15: Backend setup/ingest-key contract update: the project setup and ingest-key contract is reported implemented but not production-confirmed, so public SDK docs/examples must not claim availability yet. When backend confirms availability, SDKs should accept a project-scoped write-only ingest-key DTO with public fields such as `id`, `label`, `kind`, `created_at`, `expires_at`, and a separate raw key value for one-time setup; raw one-time keys use a distinct `lbw_ingest_` prefix and authorize telemetry only for the matching `project_id`; account/session bearer values must never be documented, printed, persisted, or reused as SDK ingest keys. Invalid, expired, or wrong-project keys should surface a redacted `ingest_key_invalid` error with an actionable next step and no echoed key text. Keep release/environment explicit in telemetry examples and canonical severity vocabulary `info`/`warning`/`error`/`critical`.
- 2026-06-15: Backend usage/limit contract update: configurable account usage enforcement is reported present in backend code but not production-confirmed, so SDK docs/examples must not claim availability yet. When backend confirms readiness, native ingest may return HTTP `429` with a redacted JSON envelope containing `code: "usage_limit_exceeded"`, `limit: "events" | "bytes"`, `reset_at`, `error`, and actionable `next`; SDKs should surface it cleanly, redact keys, avoid aggressive retry, and not derive quota locally because `GET /api/account/usage` is backend-owned. Account/session bearer values remain separate from project-scoped write-only ingest keys.
- 2026-06-15: Backend live-usage contract update: backend code reportedly publishes account usage updates after successful native ingest, but production verification is pending and no SDK implementation is requested. Future stable behavior should use backend-owned event types `usage_updated`, `usage_limit_warning`, and `usage_limit_blocked` with the same redacted payload shape as `GET /api/account/usage`; SDKs should not calculate quota locally and should keep HTTP `429` `usage_limit_exceeded` as the hard-block path that is surfaced cleanly and not retried aggressively.
- 2026-06-15: Rust Axum request integration gap reduced without adding default dependency weight. Honest status: LogBrew is now better for lightweight app-owned Axum request telemetry than a full Sentry/OpenTelemetry stack, but still worse for one-line Tower/Axum `Layer`, existing `tracing` span/log conversion, and Actix/Rocket examples. Verifier lesson: public-check tests should assert label ordering or parse the step list instead of hard-coding step numbers, because adding a legitimate smoke step shifts later step IDs. - 2026-06-15: Rust now has an optional `tower` feature with `TowerRequestTelemetryLayer`, `TowerRequestIds`, and an Axum `route_layer` example that queues the same safe request span plus `http.server.duration` metric through app-owned client state. The layer reads only W3C `traceparent`, relies on caller-provided route extraction and trace/span IDs, injects outgoing `traceparent`, ignores telemetry failures without interrupting responses, and keeps Tower/Axum/Tokio out of default installs. - 2026-06-15: Backend setup/ingest-key contract clarification: backend-owned setup progress should not be recorded until project-scoped ingest-key storage succeeds. - 2026-06-15: Rust now has an optional `tracing` feature with `LogBrewTracingLayer`, converting app-owned `tracing` events into canonical LogBrew log events without default dependency weight or arbitrary field capture. The bridge composes as a `tracing_subscriber::Layer`, accepts an app-owned timestamp function, maps trace/debug to `info`, warn to `warning`, error to `error`, captures `tracingTarget`/`tracingLevel`, and only copies primitive fields explicitly allowlisted with `with_allowed_fields(...)`; route-template fields are query/hash sanitized and debug-formatted non-primitives are ignored even when allowlisted. It does not yet convert `tracing` spans. Competitor/current signals: `sentry-tracing` supports events/breadcrumbs/logs/spans with filters and custom mapping, `tracing-opentelemetry` remains the exporter baseline, and Datadog Rust remains preview/OpenTelemetry-oriented. Local evidence: `cargo fmt --check --manifest-path rust/logbrew/Cargo.toml`, default Rust tests, all-feature Rust tests with 27 tests, `cargo clippy --manifest-path rust/logbrew/Cargo.toml --all-targets --all-features -- -D warnings`, `bash scripts/real_user_rust_tracing_smoke.sh` installed proof, and `bash scripts/real_user_rust_smoke.sh` packaged proof passed; package proof is now 24 files/179.1 KiB/36.6 KiB compressed. Next Rust gap: privacy-bounded `tracing` span conversion or Actix/Rocket examples.
- 2026-06-15: Backend setup install tracking contract: backend reports `POST /api/projects/{project_id}/setup/seen` is live for future SDK setup/init use when an SDK is initialized with a backend-minted project-scoped write-only ingest/client setup value. SDKs may call it once during setup/init, not per telemetry event; body may include `runtime` and `environment`; response is `ProjectSetupState` and may report `sdk_seen` before first telemetry. SDKs must still not accept, print, store, or repurpose account/session API values as ingest config, and public setup snippets should wait for SDK implementation around backend-minted setup values rather than adding local setup markers.
- 2026-06-16: Rust optional `tracing` bridge now supports explicit `with_span_events()` span conversion in addition to event-to-log conversion. It stays default-off, generates W3C-shaped trace/span IDs, derives parent/child links from active `tracing` spans, adds trace correlation to logs emitted inside converted spans, records span duration on close, and marks only the current span as `error` when an error-level event occurs inside it. Field capture remains primitive allowlist only, route fields are query/hash sanitized, debug-formatted non-primitives are ignored, and no payload/header/raw URL capture or subscriber replacement was added. Thermo review tightened the boundary so helper lookups pass only span correlation IDs instead of cloning full span state. Current competitor signals: Sentry `sentry-tracing` and `tracing-opentelemetry` both support richer span bridges/exporter stacks, while Datadog Rust still points toward OpenTelemetry/manual instrumentation. Local evidence: `cargo fmt --check --manifest-path rust/logbrew/Cargo.toml`, default Rust tests, all-feature Rust tests with 28 tests, `cargo clippy --manifest-path rust/logbrew/Cargo.toml --all-targets --all-features -- -D warnings`, `bash scripts/real_user_rust_tracing_smoke.sh`, `bash scripts/real_user_rust_smoke.sh`, markdown links, release metadata, backend contract reports, confidentiality scan, generated-artifact hygiene, `git diff --check`, and `cargo publish --dry-run --allow-dirty --manifest-path rust/logbrew/Cargo.toml` passed; package proof is now 24 files/189.7 KiB/38.3 KiB compressed. Honest gaps: Rust tracing span conversion is basic compared with Sentry/OTel because it does not consume an existing OTel context or model rich span events/exceptions; Actix/Rocket examples remain next Rust gaps.

- 2026-06-16: User explicitly raised tracing as the highest-value competitor gap because Sentry wins users on trace quality, and clarified this priority applies across all SDK languages, not only Rust. Treat Rust as the first concrete slice and reusable pattern, then improve tracing in popularity/evidence order across browser/JS frameworks, Node, Python, Go, Java, .NET, PHP, Ruby, mobile/native, and Rust: W3C context continuity, trace-log-error correlation, framework route spans, privacy-bounded metadata, and Sentry-level debugging usefulness without copying heavier defaults. Rust `LogBrewTracingLayer::with_span_events()` now closes one safe part by accepting explicit W3C `traceparent`/`trace_parent` fields on root `tracing` spans, continuing upstream trace ID/parent span ID, generating fresh local child span IDs, propagating sampled state into span/log metadata, ignoring malformed propagation non-fatally, and never serializing the raw propagation field. This keeps LogBrew lighter than Sentry/OpenTelemetry for app-owned Rust tracing while acknowledging remaining Rust gaps: no existing OpenTelemetry context ingestion, rich span events/exceptions, or Rocket example yet. Competitor evidence refreshed from Sentry Rust tracing/OpenTelemetry docs, `sentry-tracing`, `tracing-opentelemetry`, `OpenTelemetrySpanExt`, and OpenTelemetry context propagation docs. - 2026-06-16: Node.js tracing correlation gap reduced as the first post-Rust all-language tracing slice. Current Sentry Node docs emphasize traces that link logs for diagnostic context, OpenTelemetry JS expects active context across async execution, Node's `AsyncLocalStorage` is stable for request-lifetime state, and Datadog proves user demand through Node log/trace injection. `@logbrew/node` now attaches `logbrew.trace` for valid W3C `traceparent`, exposes `getActiveLogBrewTrace()` inside async work started by the wrapped handler, reuses the same generated request span ID for the emitted request span, and passes trace context to custom request/error/flush/failure/error callbacks. Default handler-error capture now adds `traceId`, `spanId`, `parentSpanId`, and `sampled` metadata when a request trace exists. Public docs and the first-useful Node example now use `logbrew.trace` instead of manual `parseTraceparent` in app code, and the installed smoke proves async trace preservation plus error correlation from packaged artifacts. Keep this pattern for Express/Fastify/NestJS/Next.js next, then Python web frameworks and Go/Java/.NET server helpers: expose active trace context, correlate logs/errors, stay privacy-bounded, and avoid global logger/HTTP patching by default. Local evidence: `npm --prefix js/logbrew-node test`, `python3 scripts/check_js_sources.py js/logbrew-node`, `bash scripts/check_js_lint.sh`, `bash scripts/check_js_package.sh`, and `bash scripts/real_user_node_smoke.sh` passed with Node `v22.18.0`; direct repo-root example execution failed only because bare package imports require the packaged temp app, and the installed smoke runs those examples successfully. See `docs/competitor-research/node-trace-correlation-2026-06-16.md`.
- 2026-06-16: Express tracing correlation gap reduced as the first JS framework follow-up to the Node active-trace pattern. Docs now show app-owned log correlation without raw propagation/header/body/query capture or undefined metadata fields. - 2026-06-16: NestJS tracing correlation gap reduced as the next JS framework slice. - 2026-06-16: Next.js tracing correlation gap reduced, completing the first JS server/framework active-trace sweep after Node, Express, Fastify, and NestJS. Current Sentry Next.js docs center errors/logs/traces across client/server/edge runtimes, Next.js Route Handlers use standard Web `Request`/`Response`, OpenTelemetry JS expects active async context, and Datadog confirms trace/span IDs on logs are a core debugging pivot. `@logbrew/next` now exposes `helpers.trace`, exports `getActiveLogBrewTrace()` through `AsyncLocalStorage`, reuses one route span ID across request span/app telemetry/error metadata, passes trace context to request/metric/flush/failure/error callbacks, and adds trace metadata to default route error capture. - 2026-06-16: User corrected the research bar: whenever LogBrew is behind a competitor and the competitor SDK/integration source is public, docs-only research is not enough. Future gap work must read the competitor source code first, record exact repo paths plus tags/commits and methods/classes/functions studied, summarize the design pattern and tradeoffs, then implement a lighter, safer LogBrew-native version without copying code or license text. Only skip source-level reading when the relevant source is unavailable or closed, and say that explicitly in the evidence report.
- 2026-06-16: Python/FastAPI/Django tracing correlation gap reduced after public source review of Sentry Python (`getsentry/sentry-python@1df9835e485a346f670ca5615106536a20212795`), OpenTelemetry Python contrib (`open-telemetry/opentelemetry-python-contrib@97017a46805e34faf5c181b895e002f9e0cefab5`), and Datadog `dd-trace-py` (`DataDog/dd-trace-py@96412c9279099fe5338b7104b06e65f50cac29d1`). Source paths/functions studied are recorded in `docs/competitor-research/python-trace-correlation-2026-06-16.md`. `logbrew-sdk` now has `LogBrewTraceContext` in focused `_trace_context.py`, `create_logbrew_trace_context()`, `get_active_logbrew_trace()`, `use_logbrew_trace()`, `trace_metadata()`, and `span_attributes_from_trace_context()` backed by Python `contextvars`; `LogBrewLoggingHandler` automatically adds active trace/span IDs to standard-library logs. `logbrew-fastapi` and `logbrew-django` now create one request-local W3C-shaped context per request, reuse its span ID for the request span, expose active trace during handler/view execution, and add the same IDs to captured exception issues. This keeps LogBrew lighter and more privacy-bounded than Sentry/OTel/Datadog by avoiding monkey-patching, global logger injection, payload/header/cookie/query/raw-traceparent capture, and automatic DB/template spans. Local evidence: core unittest 27 tests, `bash scripts/real_user_fastapi_smoke.sh` with `fastapi@0.137.1`, `bash scripts/real_user_django_smoke.sh` with `django@6.0.6`, `bash scripts/check_fastapi_package.sh`, `bash scripts/check_django_package.sh`, `bash scripts/check_python_static.sh`, Python source syntax, ShellCheck 0.11.0, and markdown links passed. Thermo review extracted active trace context into `_trace_context.py` so `__init__.py` stayed below 1k lines. Honest gaps: Python still lacks rich Sentry/OTel-style auto child spans, DB spans, baggage, and existing OpenTelemetry context ingestion. Backend coordination update: deployed backend reports `GET /api/account/usage/history?interval=daily|weekly|monthly|yearly` with bounded zero-filled usage buckets and actionable wrong-method envelopes for auth provider availability / telemetry ingest; SDK tooling must consume backend-owned usage/history contracts if needed later and never derive quota/history from client counters or flush state.

- 2026-06-19: Kotlin OkHttp async context gap reduced after refreshing OpenTelemetry Java instrumentation `open-telemetry/opentelemetry-java-instrumentation@8e25e07fb2bab7bd4e954d7bb744f977e9dbe785` `TracingCallFactory.newCall(...)`/`attachContextToRequest(...)`/`TracingCall.execute()`/`enqueue(...)`/callback wrappers and `TracingInterceptor.intercept(...)`, plus Sentry Java `getsentry/sentry-java@7c1a728e8bd2faa42b8f1c25c9f16a145baab60f` `SentryOkHttpInterceptor`/`SentryOkHttpEventListener`, and Datadog Android `DataDog/dd-sdk-android@519550150648592709d441c677437d8b1c3a0707` `TracingInterceptor` methods. Local evidence: TDD red failed on unchanged XHR prototype; `cd js/logbrew-react-native && npm test` (8 tests), `NPM_CONFIG_CACHE=/private/tmp/logbrew-rn-npm-cache bash scripts/real_user_react_native_smoke.sh` with `react-native@0.86.0 react@19.2.7 react-test-renderer@19.2.7`, `python3 scripts/check_js_sources.py js/logbrew-react-native`, `bash scripts/check_js_lint.sh`, `bash scripts/check_js_package.sh` (publint 0.3.21), ShellCheck 0.11.0, markdown links, confidentiality scan, generated-artifact hygiene, and diff check passed. Remaining RN gaps: default automatic instrumentation is still intentionally absent; Sentry/Datadog remain stronger for XHR response-size heuristics, richer phase timing, GraphQL-aware metadata, OTel context ingestion, source maps/native symbolication, and broader mobile/native instrumentation.
- 2026-06-23: JavaScript/Node heavy logging proof gap reduced after source reads of Sentry JavaScript `getsentry/sentry-javascript@edd901169db9e65e239858d874730a4323cafaa2` `packages/core/src/transports/base.ts` and `packages/core/src/utils/promisebuffer.ts`, Datadog Browser SDK `DataDog/browser-sdk@2536d1d26f5ac98560ac097f8e45d8a1400f1b53` `packages/browser-core/src/transport/batch.ts`/`flushController.ts`, and PostHog JS `PostHog/posthog-js@4d59d0e10f92ad3444e14dc171997c21aba57929` `packages/browser/src/request-queue.ts`. Competitors use bounded transport buffers, byte/message/time/page-exit batch controllers, or queued request batching; LogBrew now has `scripts/real_user_js_high_load_smoke.sh`, an installed-artifact temp-app smoke that installs packed `@logbrew/sdk` and `@logbrew/node`, queues 1,500 logs, proves the 1,000-event queue bound, 500 advisory `queue_overflow` drops, drop-callback isolation, local `127.0.0.1` fake intake 503-to-202 retry, trace/release/environment metadata preservation, no unsafe body content, and shutdown-after-flush behavior. It is wired into `scripts/check_public_sdks.sh` as `JavaScript high-load installed-artifact smoke` with `tests/test_js_high_load_smoke.py` and label-order coverage. Local evidence: TDD red missing script, `python3 -m unittest tests/test_js_high_load_smoke.py`, and `bash scripts/real_user_js_high_load_smoke.sh` passed after loopback sandbox escalation. Detailed report: `docs/competitor-research/js-high-load-transport-2026-06-23.md`. Remaining JS delivery gaps: byte-based batch splitting, timeout-based autonomous flush, offline persistence, and backend-owned browser unload/beacon contract.
- 2026-06-28 Node AWS SNS/EventBridge producer trace gap reduced from the source-backed Sentry JS, OpenTelemetry JS contrib, Datadog dd-trace-js, and AWS SDK evidence already recorded in `docs/competitor-research/node-sqs-tracing-2026-06-26.md`. LogBrew now adds explicit `@logbrew/aws-sqs` SNS publish, SNS publish-batch, and EventBridge PutEvents helpers plus input-cloning helpers. SNS injects one normalized W3C `traceparent` message attribute with the ten-attribute guard; EventBridge injects one `traceparent` into JSON `Detail` only when the cloned request stays under the bounded PutEvents size limit. It remains app-owned/no global AWS SDK patching and avoids payload, ARN/account, event/message ID, arbitrary attribute, baggage, and tracestate capture. Evidence: RED `bash scripts/real_user_aws_sqs_smoke.sh` failed on missing producer helper README/API surface, then package syntax, `bash scripts/real_user_aws_sqs_smoke.sh`, `python3 scripts/check_js_sources.py`, `bash scripts/check_js_lint.sh`, `bash scripts/check_js_package.sh`, markdown links, confidentiality scan, release metadata, generated-artifact hygiene, and diff check passed. The installed smoke packs local packages, proves TypeScript/ESM/CommonJS exports, SNS/EventBridge fake clients, local 503-to-202 fake-intake retry, 1,200-operation pressure path, 1,000 flushed / 200 dropped, and leakage checks. No package release yet.
- 2026-06-28 BullMQ instance instrumentation gap reduced after refreshing current Sentry JS NestJS BullMQ source (`getsentry/sentry-javascript@54e995da76381f18f61f39b0ceecadf5a0b06b11`), Datadog BullMQ plugin source (`DataDog/dd-trace-js@27dcc31908d9a6264b1536a2118534c8bc4da0f6`), and OpenTelemetry JS contrib no-BullMQ evidence (`open-telemetry/opentelemetry-js-contrib@eb98ccc85069304a1f0c2e6b33be1b2ca961b4be`). `@logbrew/bullmq` now exports `instrumentLogBrewBullMqQueue(...)`: apps pass an owned queue, LogBrew wraps only that instance's `add()`/`addBulk()`, keeps queue/Redis/worker ownership with the app, rejects duplicate install, and uninstalls cleanly. Evidence: RED installed smoke failed on missing TypeScript export, then `npm test --prefix js/logbrew-bullmq`, `bash scripts/real_user_bullmq_smoke.sh`, `python3 scripts/check_js_sources.py js/logbrew-bullmq`, JS lint/package gates, ShellCheck, markdown links, confidentiality scan, release metadata, generated-artifact hygiene, and diff check passed locally. The smoke packs local artifacts with `bullmq@5.79.1`, proves TypeScript/CJS/ESM exports, app-owned `this` binding, traceparent injection, local fake-intake flush, and no job payload leakage. Remaining BullMQ gaps: automatic NestJS processor instrumentation, hidden worker/FlowProducer hooks, data-stream monitoring, and broader auto instrumentation only in explicit framework-owned packages.
- 2026-06-28 BullMQ processor-method instrumentation gap reduced after re-reading current Sentry JS NestJS BullMQ decorator instrumentation (`packages/nestjs/src/integrations/sentry-nest-bullmq-instrumentation.ts`, `helpers.ts`) and Datadog BullMQ consumer/producer plugin source (`packages/datadog-plugin-bullmq/src/consumer.js`, `producer.js`, `test/index.spec.js`), with OpenTelemetry JS contrib still showing no first-party BullMQ instrumentation. `@logbrew/bullmq` now exports `instrumentLogBrewBullMqProcessor(...)`: apps pass an owned processor object such as a NestJS `WorkerHost` instance, LogBrew wraps only one method (default `process`), preserves the processor instance and extra args, continues the BullMQ job trace, rejects duplicate install, and uninstalls cleanly. Evidence: RED installed smoke failed on missing TypeScript export; GREEN `npm test --prefix js/logbrew-bullmq`, `bash scripts/real_user_bullmq_smoke.sh`, `python3 scripts/check_js_sources.py js/logbrew-bullmq`, JS lint/package gates, ShellCheck, markdown links, confidentiality scan, release metadata, public SDK verifier tests, generated-artifact hygiene, and diff check passed. The smoke used packed `@logbrew/sdk`, `@logbrew/node`, `@logbrew/bullmq`, `bullmq@5.79.1`, TypeScript/CJS/ESM proof, method `this`/extra-arg preservation, parent-child processor trace correlation, duplicate-install rejection, clean uninstall, local fake-intake retry/flush, and no job payload or processor error-message leakage. Remaining BullMQ gaps: Sentry remains stronger for hidden automatic NestJS decorator patching, and Datadog remains stronger for hidden worker/FlowProducer/data-stream hooks; keep LogBrew explicit unless a framework-owned integration is justified by real-user evidence.
